## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, which is a core problem in materials science and solid mechanics. Temperature typically causes thermal softening while strain causes hardening, and their interplay determines the flow stress.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic stress-strain at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * (c1 - T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon equation for plastic deformation)
- Power-law with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - T)**c3 (combined strain hardening and thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook simplified: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T) (flow stress with hardening and linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook thermal term: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - (c2 * T)**c3) (homologous temperature softening)
- Arrhenius-type: sigma = c0 * sinh(c1 * epsilon) * exp(c2 * T) (thermally activated deformation)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) * exp(c3 * T) (saturation hardening with Arrhenius thermal factor)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (power-law hardening with exponential thermal softening)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Swift model with temperature: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (shifted power law with thermal activation)
- Rational softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon / (c1 + epsilon) * (c2 - T) (saturation hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Polynomial thermoelastic: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (temperature-dependent modulus as polynomial)
- Zerilli-Armstrong type: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (thermally activated dislocation mechanics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → Stress proportional to (T_melt - T) or exp(-c*T) multiplied by strain-dependent term
- Strain hardening saturation → Voce-type form: (c0 - c1*exp(-c2*epsilon)), stress approaches asymptote at large strain
- Thermally activated deformation → Arrhenius factor exp(c*T) or exp(-c/T) multiplying a strain-dependent function
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 + f(epsilon, T), representing initial yield before hardening
- Homologous temperature scaling → Thermal softening as power of (1 - c*T) representing fraction of melting temperature
- Sinh-based flow stress → sinh(c*sigma) or inverse: sigma ~ arcsinh(f(epsilon,T)), common in creep and hot deformation models
- Competing hardening and softening → Product form: increasing function of epsilon times decreasing function of T
- Strain offset in power law → (epsilon + c)**n instead of epsilon**n to avoid singularity at zero strain and represent pre-strain
